"Introduction (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<p>This deck has taken definitions outlined in <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory"">Wikipedia's Glossary of category theory</a> and put them into a form which can be easily learnt/revised using <a href=""https://apps.ankiweb.net/"">Anki</a> a cross platform app specifically designed for long term knowledge retention.</p>
<h2>Notes</h2>
<p>Please note the modifications which have been made &amp; where you can find updates.</p>
<ol align=""left"">
<li>The front of every card has ""(Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"" appended to the end so that if you have any other words in your collection, the Wikipedia definition will still be added when importing it.</li>
<li>Any updates or corrections to the deck will be available at <a href=""https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Category-Theory-Flashcards"">https://github.com/darigovresearch/Wikipedia-Glossary-of-Category-Theory-Flashcards</a> so do return periodically to check if you have the latest version.</li>
</ol>
<p>Feel free to share the deck and give the repository a star so more people are likely to see this work and can get the most out of it.</p>

"
"abelian (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abelian_category"" title=""Abelian category"">abelian</a> if it has a zero object, it has all pullbacks and pushouts, and all monomorphisms and epimorphisms are normal.
"
"accessible (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Given a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardinal_number"" title=""Cardinal number"">cardinal number</a> κ, an object <i>X</i> in a category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accessible_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Accessible object"">κ-accessible</a> (or κ-compact or κ-presentable) if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (X,-)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>Hom</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (X,-)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ff04322e141ee468880e85236e7ed322d81f4b66"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.473ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} (X,-)""/></span> commutes with κ-filtered colimits.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;Given a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regular_cardinal"" title=""Regular cardinal"">regular cardinal</a> κ, a category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accessible_category"" title=""Accessible category"">κ-accessible</a> if it has κ-filtered colimits and there exists a small set <i>S</i> of κ-compact objects that generates the category under colimits, meaning every object can be written as a colimit of diagrams of objects in <i>S</i>.</dd>
"
"additive (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Additive_category"" title=""Additive category"">additive</a> if it is preadditive (to be precise, has some pre-additive structure) and admits all finite <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coproduct"" title=""Coproduct"">coproducts</a>. Although ""preadditive"" is an additional structure, one can show ""additive"" is a <i>property</i> of a category; i.e., one can ask whether a given category is additive or not.<sup id=""cite_ref-2"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-2"">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
"
"adjunction (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adjoint_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Adjoint functor"">adjunction</a> (also called an adjoint pair) is a pair of functors <i>F</i>: <i>C</i> → <i>D</i>, <i>G</i>: <i>D</i> → <i>C</i> such that there is a ""natural"" bijection
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} _{D}(F(X),Y)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(X,G(Y))}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">

          <mi>Hom</mi>

        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>&#x2243;<!-- ≃ --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Hom</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} _{D}(F(X),Y)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(X,G(Y))}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0258fb8922a809b57061db833bcc03e86c771255"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:36.235ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} _{D}(F(X),Y)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(X,G(Y))""/></span>;</dd></dl>
<i>F</i> is said to be left adjoint to <i>G</i> and <i>G</i> to right adjoint to <i>F</i>. Here, ""natural"" means there is a natural isomorphism <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} _{D}(F(-),-)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(-,G(-))}"">

        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>

            <mi>C</mi>

        </msub>

        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>

        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>

"
"algebra for a monad (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a monad <i>T</i> in a category <i>X</i>, an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebra_for_a_monad"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Algebra for a monad"">algebra for <i>T</i></a> or a <i>T</i>-algebra is an object in <i>X</i> with a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoid_action"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monoid action"">monoid action</a> of <i>T</i> (""algebra"" is misleading and ""<i>T</i>-object"" is perhaps a better term.) For example, given a group <i>G</i> that determines a monad <i>T</i> in <b>Set</b> in the standard way, a <i>T</i>-algebra is a set with an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_action_(mathematics)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Group action (mathematics)"">action</a> of <i>G</i>.
"
"amnestic (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor is amnestic if it has the property: if <i>k</i> is an isomorphism and <i>F</i>(<i>k</i>) is an identity, then <i>k</i> is an identity."
"balanced (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is balanced if every bimorphism is an isomorphism.
"
"Beck's theorem (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beck%27s_monadicity_theorem"" title=""Beck&#39;s monadicity theorem"">Beck's theorem</a> characterizes the category of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebra_for_a_monad"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Algebra for a monad"">algebras for a given monad</a>.
"
"bicategory (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicategory"" title=""Bicategory"">bicategory</a> is a model of a weak <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2-category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""2-category"">2-category</a>.
"
"bifunctor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bifunctor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bifunctor"">bifunctor</a> from a pair of categories <i>C</i> and <i>D</i> to a category <i>E</i> is a functor <i>C</i> × <i>D</i> → <i>E</i>. For example, for any category <i>C</i>, <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (-,-)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>Hom</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (-,-)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/109100e375473e3b95c60a7ebf1adc71ce797c04"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.301ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} (-,-)""/></span> is a bifunctor from <i>C</i><sup>op</sup> and <i>C</i> to <b>Set</b>.
"
"bimorphism (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bimorphism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bimorphism"">bimorphism</a> is a morphism that is both an epimorphism and a monomorphism.
"
"Bousfield localization (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bousfield_localization"" title=""Bousfield localization"">Bousfield localization</a>.
"
"calculus of functors (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculus_of_functors"" title=""Calculus of functors"">calculus of functors</a> is a technique of studying functors in the manner similar to the way a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(mathematics)"" title=""Function (mathematics)"">function</a> is studied via its <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taylor_series"" title=""Taylor series"">Taylor series</a> expansion; whence, the term ""calculus"".
"
"cartesian closed (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartesian_closed_category"" title=""Cartesian closed category"">cartesian closed</a> if it has a terminal object and that any two objects have a product and exponential.
"
"cartesian functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given relative categories <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle p:F\to C,q:G\to C}"">

    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">

        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>q</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle p:F\to C,q:G\to C}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/314cafcf4d6d17fbb197dbfb88bc89c86443d04c"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:21.565ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle p:F\to C,q:G\to C}""/></span> over the same base category <i>C</i>, a functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:F\to G}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">

        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f:F\to G}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/85edcca983d67148f3ef74994f52e81db9fa9a81"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.397ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f:F\to G""/></span> over <i>C</i> is cartesian if it sends cartesian morphisms to cartesian morphisms.
"
"cartesian morphism (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;Given a functor π: <i>C</i> → <i>D</i> (e.g., a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prestack"" title=""Prestack"">prestack</a> over schemes), a morphism <i>f</i>: <i>x</i> → <i>y</i> in <i>C</i> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartesian_morphism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cartesian morphism"">π-cartesian</a> if, for each object <i>z</i> in <i>C</i>, each morphism <i>g</i>: <i>z</i> → <i>y</i> in <i>C</i> and each morphism <i>v</i>: π(<i>z</i>) → π(<i>x</i>) in <i>D</i> such that π(<i>g</i>) = π(<i>f</i>) ∘ <i>v</i>, there exists a unique morphism <i>u</i>: <i>z</i> → <i>x</i> such that π(<i>u</i>) = <i>v</i> and <i>g</i> = <i>f</i> ∘ <i>u</i>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;Given a functor π: <i>C</i> → <i>D</i> (e.g., a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prestack"" title=""Prestack"">prestack</a> over rings), a morphism <i>f</i>: <i>x</i> → <i>y</i> in <i>C</i> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartesian_morphism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Cartesian morphism"">π-coCartesian</a> if, for each object <i>z</i> in <i>C</i>, each morphism <i>g</i>: <i>x</i> → <i>z</i> in <i>C</i> and each morphism <i>v</i>: π(<i>y</i>) → π(<i>z</i>) in <i>D</i> such that π(<i>g</i>) = <i>v</i> ∘ π(<i>f</i>), there exists a unique morphism <i>u</i>: <i>y</i> → <i>z</i> such that π(<i>u</i>) = <i>v</i> and <i>g</i> = <i>u</i>  ∘ <i>f</i>. (In short, <i>f</i> is the dual of a π-cartesian morphism.)</dd>
"
"Cartesian square (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A commutative diagram that is isomorphic to the diagram given as a fiber product.
"
"categorical logic (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Categorical_logic"" title=""Categorical logic"">Categorical logic</a> is an approach to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_logic"" title=""Mathematical logic"">mathematical logic</a> that uses category theory.
"
"categorification (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Categorification"" title=""Categorification"">Categorification</a> is a process of replacing sets and set-theoretic concepts with categories and category-theoretic concepts in some nontrivial way to capture categoric flavors. Decategorification is the reverse of categorification.
"
"category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_(mathematics)"" title=""Category (mathematics)"">category</a> consists of the following data

<li>For each pair of objects <i>X</i>, <i>Y</i>, a set <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (X,Y)}"">

<li>For each triple of objects <i>X</i>, <i>Y</i>, <i>Z</i>, a map (called composition)

</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4779b7635d2828567e3d682af101abd927b3157a"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:58.338ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\circ :\operatorname {Hom} (Y,Z)\times \operatorname {Hom} (X,Y)\to \operatorname {Hom} (X,Z),\,(g,f)\mapsto g\circ f""/></span>,</dd></dl></li>
<li>For each object <i>X</i>, an identity morphism <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {id} _{X}\in \operatorname {Hom} (X,X)}"">

        <msub>
          <mi>id</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
        <mi>Hom</mi>

subject to the conditions: for any morphisms <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:X\to Y}"">

<ul><li><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle (h\circ g)\circ f=h\circ (g\circ f)}"">

      </mstyle>

For example, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partially_ordered_set"" title=""Partially ordered set"">partially ordered set</a> can be viewed as a category: the objects are the elements of the set and for each pair of objects <i>x</i>, <i>y</i>, there is a unique morphism <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle x\to y}"">

      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle x\to y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/43570cdee5baeaebcf546338f77cf67c27a7344f"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.099ex; height:2.176ex;"" alt=""x\to y""/></span> if and only if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle x\leq y}"">

        <mi>y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle x\leq y}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c07a0bc023490be1c08e6c33a9cdc93bec908224"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.584ex; height:2.343ex;"" alt=""x\leq y""/></span>; the associativity of composition means transitivity.
"
"category of categories (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_categories"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Category of categories"">category of (small) categories</a>, denoted by <b>Cat</b>, is a category where the objects are all the categories which are small with respect to some fixed universe and the morphisms are all the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functor"" title=""Functor"">functors</a>.
"
"classifying space (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classifying_space_of_a_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Classifying space of a category"">classifying space of a category</a> <i>C</i> is the geometric realization of the nerve of <i>C</i>.
"
"co (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Often used synonymous with op-; for example, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colimit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Colimit"">colimit</a> refers to an op-limit in the sense that it is a limit in the opposite category. But there might be a distinction; for example, an op-fibration is not the same thing as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cofibration"" title=""Cofibration"">cofibration</a>.
"
"coend (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The coend of a functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle F:C^{\text{op}}\times C\to X}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>C</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mtext>op</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle F:C^{\text{op}}\times C\to X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7d29c0e3cc0f008cb97387d2fbe219cbf04cb459"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:17.645ex; height:2.343ex;"" alt=""F:C^{\text{op}}\times C\to X""/></span> is the dual of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/End_(category_theory)"" title=""End (category theory)"">end</a> of <i>F</i> and is denoted by
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \int ^{c\in C}F(c,c)}"">

      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">

          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>c</mi>
            <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>c</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>c</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \int ^{c\in C}F(c,c)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e79bba45ccf2e453f3bc647a0c40ffe8a984ab5d"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:12.738ex; height:6.343ex;"" alt=""\int ^{c\in C}F(c,c)""/></span>.</dd></dl>
For example, if <i>R</i> is a ring, <i>M</i> a right <i>R</i>-module and <i>N</i> a left <i>R</i>-module, then the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tensor_product_of_modules"" title=""Tensor product of modules"">tensor product</a> of <i>M</i> and <i>N</i> is
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle M\otimes _{R}N=\int ^{R}M\otimes _{\mathbb {Z} }N}"">

            <mi>R</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>N</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <msup>
          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- ∫ --></mo>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>R</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mi>M</mi>
        <msub>
          <mo>&#x2297;<!-- ⊗ --></mo>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
              <mi mathvariant=""double-struck"">Z</mi>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>N</mi>
      </mstyle>

  </semantics>

where <i>R</i> is viewed as a category with one object whose morphisms are the elements of <i>R</i>.
"
"coequalizer (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coequalizer"" title=""Coequalizer"">coequalizer</a> of a pair of morphisms <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f,g:A\to B}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>B</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f,g:A\to B}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/17911b4e8e6a2f58d32826d24e9f879918303975"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.487ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f,g:A\to B""/></span> is the colimit of the pair. It is the dual of an equalizer.
"
"coherence theorem (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coherence_theorem"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Coherence theorem"">coherence theorem</a> is a theorem of a form that states a weak structure is equivalent to a strict structure.
"
"coimage (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coimage"" title=""Coimage"">coimage</a> of a morphism <i>f</i>: <i>X</i> → <i>Y</i> is the coequalizer of <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle X\times _{Y}X\rightrightarrows X}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>X</mi>
        <msub>
          <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>Y</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x21C9;<!-- ⇉ --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle X\times _{Y}X\rightrightarrows X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5e337c62274495d62f3a2675751d7ff1f9a2e415"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.881ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle X\times _{Y}X\rightrightarrows X}""/></span>.
"
"colored operad (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Another term for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicategory"" title=""Multicategory"">multicategory</a>, a generalized category where a morphism can have several domains. The notion of ""colored operad"" is more primitive than that of operad: in fact, an operad can be defined as a colored operad with a single object.
"
"comma (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given functors <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:C\to B,g:D\to B}"">
  <semantics>

        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>D</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>B</mi>

  <semantics>

"
"comonad (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comonad"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Comonad"">comonad</a> in a category <i>X</i> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comonoid"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Comonoid"">comonoid</a> in the monoidal category of endofunctors of <i>X</i>.
"
"compact (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Probably synonymous with <a href=""#accessible"">#accessible</a>.
"
"complete (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complete_category"" title=""Complete category"">complete</a> if all small limits exist.
"
"composition (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A composition of morphisms in a category is part of the datum defining the category.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;If <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:C\to D,\,g:D\to E}"">

"concrete (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concrete_category"" title=""Concrete category"">concrete category</a> <i>C</i> is a category such that there is a faithful functor from <i>C</i> to <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_sets"" title=""Category of sets"">Set</a></b>; e.g., <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_vector_spaces"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Category of vector spaces"">Vec</a></b>, <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_groups"" title=""Category of groups"">Grp</a></b> and <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_topological_spaces"" title=""Category of topological spaces"">Top</a></b>.
"
"cone (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cone_(category_theory)"" title=""Cone (category theory)"">cone</a> is a way to express the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_property"" title=""Universal property"">universal property</a> of a colimit (or dually a limit). One can show<sup id=""cite_ref-3"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-3"">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> that the colimit <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \varinjlim }"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-OP"">
          <munder>
            <mi>lim</mi>
            <mo>&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
          </munder>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \varinjlim }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0753732a44a7b3d11249c0b1f344a457a3cb7178"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -1.637ex; margin-bottom: -0.367ex; width:3.36ex; height:3.843ex;"" alt=""\varinjlim ""/></span> is the left adjoint to the diagonal functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \Delta :C\to \operatorname {Fct} (I,C)}"">

        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>

        <mi>Fct</mi>

    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f:I\to C}</annotation>

</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9271e0d23650020d206dcdb2277513962308597f"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.768ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f:I\to C""/></span>,
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (\varinjlim f,X)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} (f,\Delta _{X}),}"">

        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-OP"">
          <munder>
            <mi>lim</mi>
            <mo>&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
          </munder>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>&#x2243;<!-- ≃ --></mo>
        <mi>Hom</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant=""normal"">&#x0394;<!-- Δ --></mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (\varinjlim f,X)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} (f,\Delta _{X}),}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ef2f41a7c0f4f5927c41927d8efbe87343a81fcc"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -1.637ex; margin-bottom: -0.367ex; width:30.967ex; height:4.009ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} (\varinjlim f,X)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} (f,\Delta _{X}),""/></span></dd></dl>
provided the colimit in question exists. The right-hand side is then the set of cones with vertex <i>X</i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-4"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-4"">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>

"connected (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"

"
"conservative functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservative_functor"" title=""Conservative functor"">conservative functor</a> is a functor that reflects isomorphisms. Many forgetful functors are conservative, but the forgetful functor from <b>Top</b> to <b>Set</b> is not conservative.
"
"constant (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constant_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Constant functor"">constant</a> if it maps every object in a category to the same object <i>A</i> and every morphism to the identity on <i>A</i>. Put in another way, a functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:C\to D}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>D</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f:C\to D}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9af673473fce78b42b08129374eef6a040b35bb"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.52ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f:C\to D""/></span> is constant if it factors as: <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle C\to \{A\}{\overset {i}{\to }}D}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>C</mi>

        <mo fence=""false"" stretchy=""false"">{</mo>

"contravariant functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contravariant_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Contravariant functor"">contravariant functor</a> <i>F</i> from a category <i>C</i> to a category <i>D</i> is a (covariant) functor from <i>C</i><sup>op</sup> to <i>D</i>. It is sometimes also called a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presheaf_(category_theory)"" title=""Presheaf (category theory)"">presheaf</a> especially when <i>D</i> is <b>Set</b> or the variants. For example, for each set <i>S</i>, let <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle {\mathfrak {P}}(S)}"">

"coproduct (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coproduct"" title=""Coproduct"">coproduct</a> of a family of objects <i>X</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> in a category <i>C</i> indexed by a set <i>I</i> is the inductive limit <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \varinjlim }"">

        </mrow>

It is the dual of the product of the family. For example, a coproduct in <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_groups"" title=""Category of groups"">Grp</a></b> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_product"" title=""Free product"">free product</a>.
"
"core (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Core_(category_theory)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Core (category theory) (page does not exist)"">core</a> of a category is the maximal groupoid contained in the category.
"

          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">c</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">t</mi>
        </mrow>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>M</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">S</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">e</mi>

"
"density theorem (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Density_theorem_(category_theory)"" title=""Density theorem (category theory)"">density theorem</a> states that every presheaf (a set-valued contravariant functor) is a colimit of representable presheaves. Yoneda's lemma embeds a category <i>C</i> into the category of presheaves on <i>C</i>. The density theorem then says the image is ""dense"", so to say. The name ""density"" is because of the analogy with the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacobson_density_theorem"" title=""Jacobson density theorem"">Jacobson density theorem</a> (or other variants) in abstract algebra.
"
"diagonal functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given categories <i>I</i>, <i>C</i>, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diagonal_functor"" title=""Diagonal functor"">diagonal functor</a> is the functor
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \Delta :C\to \mathbf {Fct} (I,C),\,A\mapsto \Delta _{A}}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi mathvariant=""normal"">&#x0394;<!-- Δ --></mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">F</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">c</mi>

"
"diagram (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a category <i>C</i>, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diagram_(category_theory)"" title=""Diagram (category theory)"">diagram</a> in <i>C</i> is a functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:I\to C}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>I</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f:I\to C}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9271e0d23650020d206dcdb2277513962308597f"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.768ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f:I\to C""/></span> from a small category <i>I</i>.
"
"differential graded category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_graded_category"" title=""Differential graded category"">differential graded category</a> is a category whose Hom sets are equipped with structures of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_graded_module"" title=""Differential graded module"">differential graded modules</a>. In particular, if the category has only one object, it is the same as a differential graded module.
"
"direct limit (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_limit"" title=""Direct limit"">direct limit</a> is the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colimit"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Colimit"">colimit</a> of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_system"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Direct system"">direct system</a>.
"
"discrete (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discrete_category"" title=""Discrete category"">discrete</a> if each morphism is an identity morphism (of some object). For example, a set can be viewed as a discrete category.
"
"distributor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Another term for ""profunctor"".
"
"Dwyer–Kan equivalence (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dwyer%E2%80%93Kan_equivalence&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Dwyer–Kan equivalence (page does not exist)"">Dwyer–Kan equivalence</a> is a generalization of an equivalence of categories to the simplicial context.<sup id=""cite_ref-6"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-6"">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>"
"Eilenberg–Moore category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Another name for the category of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebra_for_a_monad"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Algebra for a monad"">algebras for a given monad</a>.
"
"empty (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empty_category_(category_theory)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Empty category (category theory)"">empty category</a> is a category with no object. It is the same thing as the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empty_set"" title=""Empty set"">empty set</a> when the empty set is viewed as a discrete category.
"

        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle F,G:C\to X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bd16f8e936ee4620154a13ed87c48b2b6c6cf165"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.899ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""F,G:C\to X""/></span>,
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \int _{c\in C}\operatorname {Hom} (F(c),G(c))}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msub>
          <mo>&#x222B;<!-- ∫ --></mo>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>c</mi>
            <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>Hom</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>c</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>c</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \int _{c\in C}\operatorname {Hom} (F(c),G(c))}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/85cf0a5a6aec09700ea29be3f20b8f6d16247734"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:21.854ex; height:5.676ex;"" alt=""\int _{c\in C}\operatorname {Hom} (F(c),G(c))""/></span></dd></dl>
is the set of natural transformations from <i>F</i> to <i>G</i>. For more examples, see <a rel=""nofollow"" class=""external text"" href=""https://mathoverflow.net/q/78471"">this mathoverflow thread</a>. The dual of an end is a coend.
"
"endofunctor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor between the same category.
"
"enriched category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a monoidal category (<i>C</i>, ⊗, 1), a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_enriched"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Category enriched"">category enriched</a> over <i>C</i> is, informally, a category whose Hom sets are in <i>C</i>. More precisely, a category <i>D</i> enriched over <i>C</i> is a data consisting of
<ol><li>A class of objects,</li>
<li>For each pair of objects <i>X</i>, <i>Y</i> in <i>D</i>, an object <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Y)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>D</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Y)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ed9fe2e2ad1016bcb589421adadf9555d9b8b2ac"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.775ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Y)}""/></span> in <i>C</i>, called the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mapping_object&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Mapping object (page does not exist)"">mapping object</a> from <i>X</i> to <i>Y</i>,</li>
<li>For each triple of objects <i>X</i>, <i>Y</i>, <i>Z</i> in <i>D</i>, a morphism in <i>C</i>,
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \circ :\operatorname {Map} _{D}(Y,Z)\otimes \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Y)\to \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Z)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>D</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Z</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>&#x2297;<!-- ⊗ --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>D</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>D</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Z</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \circ :\operatorname {Map} _{D}(Y,Z)\otimes \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Y)\to \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Z)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ee45f19fef49a1a3d5c90915ef985b3b8926d739"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:47.488ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle \circ :\operatorname {Map} _{D}(Y,Z)\otimes \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Y)\to \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,Z)}""/></span>,</dd>
<dd>called the composition,</dd></dl></li>
<li>For each object <i>X</i> in <i>D</i>, a morphism <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle 1_{X}:1\to \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,X)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msub>
          <mn>1</mn>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>D</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle 1_{X}:1\to \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,X)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2aa9cc409d56636d58610189805d7db82ba4e723"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:22.491ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle 1_{X}:1\to \operatorname {Map} _{D}(X,X)}""/></span> in <i>C</i>, called the unit morphism of <i>X</i></li></ol>
subject to the conditions that (roughly) the compositions are associative and the unit morphisms act as the multiplicative identity.

For example, a category enriched over sets is an ordinary category.
"
"epimorphism (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A morphism <i>f</i> is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epimorphism"" title=""Epimorphism"">epimorphism</a> if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle g=h}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>h</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle g=h}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/50f4fd70b1200ffb96f9b7dccc5b64296e8da9f4"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.553ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""g=h""/></span> whenever <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle g\circ f=h\circ f}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>h</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle g\circ f=h\circ f}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6684a08ba3c9d443fa7fd91c5da2831846cd4f4e"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.5ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""g\circ f=h\circ f""/></span>. In other words, <i>f</i> is the dual of a monomorphism.
"
"equalizer (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equalizer_(mathematics)"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Equalizer (mathematics)"">equalizer</a> of a pair of morphisms <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f,g:A\to B}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>B</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f,g:A\to B}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/17911b4e8e6a2f58d32826d24e9f879918303975"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.487ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f,g:A\to B""/></span> is the limit of the pair. It is the dual of a coequalizer.
"
"equivalence (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A functor is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalence_of_categories"" title=""Equivalence of categories"">equivalence</a> if it is faithful, full and essentially surjective.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A morphism in an ∞-category <i>C</i>  is an equivalence if it gives an isomorphism in the homotopy category of <i>C</i>.</dd>
"
"equivalent (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is equivalent to another category if there is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equivalence_of_categories"" title=""Equivalence of categories"">equivalence</a> between them.
"
"essentially surjective (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor <i>F</i> is called <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Essentially_surjective&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Essentially surjective (page does not exist)"">essentially surjective</a> (or isomorphism-dense) if for every object <i>B</i> there exists an object <i>A</i> such that <i>F</i>(<i>A</i>) is isomorphic to <i>B</i>.
"
"evaluation (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given categories <i>C</i>, <i>D</i> and an object <i>A</i> in <i>C</i>, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Evaluation_(category_theory)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Evaluation (category theory) (page does not exist)"">evaluation</a> at <i>A</i> is the functor
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \mathbf {Fct} (C,D)\to D,\,\,F\mapsto F(A).}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">F</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">c</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">t</mi>
        </mrow>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>D</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>D</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mspace width=""thinmathspace"" />
        <mspace width=""thinmathspace"" />
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x21A6;<!-- ↦ --></mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \mathbf {Fct} (C,D)\to D,\,\,F\mapsto F(A).}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/baf3f750d84d4ff1cef0ce11e3f13902d2dda7c0"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:29.085ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle \mathbf {Fct} (C,D)\to D,\,\,F\mapsto F(A).}""/></span></dd></dl>
For example, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eilenberg%E2%80%93Steenrod_axioms"" title=""Eilenberg–Steenrod axioms"">Eilenberg–Steenrod axioms</a> give an instance when the functor is an equivalence."
"faithful (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faithful_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Faithful functor"">faithful</a> if it is injective when restricted to each <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hom-set"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hom-set"">hom-set</a>.
"

"
"fibered category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor π: <i>C</i> → <i>D</i> is said to exhibit <i>C</i> as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibered_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fibered category"">category fibered over</a> <i>D</i> if, for each morphism <i>g</i>: <i>x</i> → π(<i>y</i>) in <i>D</i>, there exists a π-cartesian morphism <i>f</i>: <i>x'</i> → <i>y</i> in <i>C</i> such that π(<i>f</i>) = <i>g</i>. If <i>D</i> is the category of affine schemes (say of finite type over some field), then π is more commonly called a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prestack"" title=""Prestack"">prestack</a>. <b>Note</b>: π is often a forgetful functor and in fact the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck_construction"" title=""Grothendieck construction"">Grothendieck construction</a> implies that every fibered category can be taken to be that form (up to equivalences in a suitable sense).
"
"fiber product (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a category <i>C</i> and a set <i>I</i>, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiber_product"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fiber product"">fiber product</a> over an object <i>S</i> of a family of objects <i>X</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> in <i>C</i> indexed by <i>I</i> is the product of the family in the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slice_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Slice category"">slice category</a> <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle C_{/S}}"">

"filtered (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filtered_category"" title=""Filtered category"">filtered category</a> (also called a filtrant category) is a nonempty category with the properties (1) given objects <i>i</i> and <i>j</i>, there are an object <i>k</i> and morphisms <i>i</i> → <i>k</i> and <i>j</i> → <i>k</i> and (2) given morphisms <i>u</i>, <i>v</i>: <i>i</i> → <i>j</i>, there are an object <i>k</i> and a morphism <i>w</i>: <i>j</i> → <i>k</i> such that <i>w</i> ∘ <i>u</i> = <i>w</i> ∘ <i>v</i>. A category <i>I</i> is filtered if and only if, for each finite category <i>J</i> and functor <i>f</i>: <i>J</i> → <i>I</i>, the set <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \varprojlim \operatorname {Hom} (f(j),i)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">

        <mi>i</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f88ebf341bdcdf3bb993a6d22a51acb022b2b3b2"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -1.637ex; margin-bottom: -0.367ex; width:16.345ex; height:4.009ex;"" alt=""\varprojlim \operatorname {Hom} (f(j),i)""/></span> is nonempty for some object <i>i</i> in <i>I</i>.</dd>
"
"finitary monad (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Finitary_monad&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Finitary monad (page does not exist)"">finitary monad</a> or an algebraic monad is a monad on <b>Set</b> whose underlying endofunctor commutes with filtered colimits.
"
"finite (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is finite if it has only finitely many morphisms.
"
"forgetful functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forgetful_functor"" title=""Forgetful functor"">forgetful functor</a> is, roughly, a functor that loses some of data of the objects; for example, the functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \mathbf {Grp} \to \mathbf {Set} }"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">G</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">r</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">p</mi>
        </mrow>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">S</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">e</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">t</mi>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \mathbf {Grp} \to \mathbf {Set} }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/30dbb1a1256ddef855212e8e5d28764c4d22e0ef"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.052ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""\mathbf {Grp} \to \mathbf {Set} ""/></span> that sends a group to its underlying set and a group homomorphism to itself is a forgetful functor.
"
"free functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Free functor"">free functor</a> is a left adjoint to a forgetful functor. For example, for a ring <i>R</i>, the functor that sends a set <i>X</i> to the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_module"" title=""Free module"">free <i>R</i>-module</a> generated by <i>X</i> is a free functor (whence the name).
"
"Frobenius category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frobenius_category"" title=""Frobenius category"">Frobenius category</a> is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exact_category"" title=""Exact category"">exact category</a> that has enough injectives and enough projectives and such that the class of injective objects coincides with that of projective objects.
"
"Fukaya category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fukaya_category"" title=""Fukaya category"">Fukaya category</a>.
"
"full (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A functor is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Full functor"">full</a> if it is surjective when restricted to each <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hom-set"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Hom-set"">hom-set</a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A category <i>A</i> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_subcategory"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Full subcategory"">full subcategory</a> of a category <i>B</i> if the inclusion functor from <i>A</i> to <i>B</i> is full.</dd>
"
"functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given categories <i>C</i>, <i>D</i>, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functor"" title=""Functor"">functor</a> <i>F</i> from <i>C</i> to <i>D</i> is a structure-preserving map from <i>C</i> to <i>D</i>; i.e., it consists of an object <i>F</i>(<i>x</i>) in <i>D</i> for each object <i>x</i> in <i>C</i> and a morphism <i>F</i>(<i>f</i>) in <i>D</i> for each morphism <i>f</i> in <i>C</i> satisfying the conditions: (1) <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle F(f\circ g)=F(f)\circ F(g)}"">

        <mi>g</mi>

"functor category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functor_category"" title=""Functor category"">functor category</a> <b>Fct</b>(<i>C</i>, <i>D</i>) or <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle D^{C}}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msup>
          <mi>D</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle D^{C}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/108456f7fa636edcc6227f68cd48cade449ab356"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.406ex; height:2.676ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle D^{C}}""/></span> from a category <i>C</i> to a category <i>D</i> is the category where the objects are all the functors from <i>C</i> to <i>D</i> and the morphisms are all the natural transformations between the functors.
"
"Gabriel–Popescu theorem (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabriel%E2%80%93Popescu_theorem"" title=""Gabriel–Popescu theorem"">Gabriel–Popescu theorem</a> says an abelian category is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serre_quotient_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Serre quotient category"">quotient</a> of the category of modules.
"

"Grothendieck's Galois theory (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category-theoretic generalization of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galois_theory"" title=""Galois theory"">Galois theory</a>; see <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck%27s_Galois_theory"" title=""Grothendieck&#39;s Galois theory"">Grothendieck's Galois theory</a>.
"
"Grothendieck category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck_category"" title=""Grothendieck category"">Grothendieck category</a> is a certain well-behaved kind of an abelian category.
"
"Grothendieck construction (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle U:C\to \mathbf {Cat} }"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>U</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">C</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">a</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">t</mi>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle U:C\to \mathbf {Cat} }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/75b03cd393ad3644f3c186164e5ce294e34147f3"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:13.37ex; height:2.176ex;"" alt=""U:C\to \mathbf {Cat} ""/></span>, let <i>D</i><sub><i>U</i></sub> be the category where the objects are pairs (<i>x</i>, <i>u</i>) consisting of an object <i>x</i> in <i>C</i> and an object <i>u</i> in the category <i>U</i>(<i>x</i>) and a morphism from (<i>x</i>, <i>u</i>) to (<i>y</i>, <i>v</i>) is a pair consisting of a morphism <i>f</i>: <i>x</i> → <i>y</i> in <i>C</i> and a morphism <i>U</i>(<i>f</i>)(<i>u</i>) → <i>v</i> in <i>U</i>(<i>y</i>). The passage from <i>U</i> to <i>D</i><sub><i>U</i></sub> is then called the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck_construction"" title=""Grothendieck construction"">Grothendieck construction</a>.
"
"Grothendieck fibration (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibered_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Fibered category"">fibered category</a>.
"
"groupoid (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A category is called a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groupoid"" title=""Groupoid"">groupoid</a> if every morphism in it is an isomorphism.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An ∞-category is called an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E2%88%9E-groupoid"" title=""∞-groupoid"">∞-groupoid</a> if every morphism in it is an equivalence (or equivalently if it is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kan_complex"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Kan complex"">Kan complex</a>.)</dd>
"
"Hall algebra of a category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ringel%E2%80%93Hall_algebra"" title=""Ringel–Hall algebra"">Ringel–Hall algebra</a>.
"

"
"Higher category theory (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher_category_theory"" title=""Higher category theory"">Higher category theory</a> is a subfield of category theory that concerns the study of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/N-category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""N-category""><i>n</i>-categories</a> and <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E2%88%9E-categories"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""∞-categories"">∞-categories</a>.
"
"homological dimension (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homological_dimension"" title=""Homological dimension"">homological dimension</a> of an abelian category with enough injectives is the least non-negativer integer <i>n</i> such that every object in the category admits an injective resolution of length at most <i>n</i>. The dimension is ∞ if no such integer exists. For example, the homological dimension of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_modules"" title=""Category of modules"">Mod<sub><i>R</i></sub></a> with a principal ideal domain <i>R</i> is at most one.
"
"homotopy category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homotopy_category"" title=""Homotopy category"">homotopy category</a>. It is closely related to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Localization_of_a_category"" title=""Localization of a category"">localization of a category</a>.
"
"homotopy hypothesis (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homotopy_hypothesis"" title=""Homotopy hypothesis"">homotopy hypothesis</a> states an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E2%88%9E-groupoid"" title=""∞-groupoid"">∞-groupoid</a> is a space (less equivocally, an <i>n</i>-groupoid can be used as a homotopy <i>n</i>-type.)"
"identity (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_morphism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Identity morphism"">identity morphism</a> <i>f</i> of an object <i>A</i> is a morphism from <i>A</i> to <i>A</i> such that for any morphisms <i>g</i> with domain <i>A</i> and <i>h</i> with codomain <i>A</i>, <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle g\circ f=g}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle g\circ f=g}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9bcac3b4321d1d8960b4aa35d19377410cbca08a"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.804ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""g\circ f=g""/></span> and <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f\circ h=h}"">

<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Identity functor"">identity functor</a> on a category <i>C</i> is a functor from <i>C</i> to <i>C</i> that sends objects and morphisms to themselves.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">3.&#160;&#160;Given a functor <i>F</i>: <i>C</i> → <i>D</i>, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_natural_transformation"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Identity natural transformation"">identity natural transformation</a> from <i>F</i> to <i>F</i> is a natural transformation consisting of the identity morphisms of <i>F</i>(<i>X</i>) in <i>D</i> for the objects <i>X</i> in <i>C</i>.</dd>

"∞-category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E2%88%9E-category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""∞-category"">∞-category</a> <i>C</i> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_set"" title=""Simplicial set"">simplicial set</a> satisfying the following condition: for each 0 &lt; <i>i</i> &lt; <i>n</i>,
<ul><li>every map of simplicial sets <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:\Lambda _{i}^{n}\to C}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <msubsup>
          <mi mathvariant=""normal"">&#x039B;<!-- Λ --></mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>n</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msubsup>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f:\Lambda _{i}^{n}\to C}</annotation>
  </semantics>

          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">

          </mrow>

        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>

where &#916;<sup><i>n</i></sup> is the standard <i>n</i>-simplex and <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \Lambda _{i}^{n}}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
