            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>n</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msubsup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \Lambda _{i}^{n}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e83ace72faae848b80156cd2412a563ba8a7b0d2"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.832ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\Lambda _{i}^{n}""/></span> is obtained from &#916;<sup><i>n</i></sup> by removing the <i>i</i>-th face and the interior (see <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kan_fibration#Definition"" title=""Kan fibration"">Kan fibration#Definition</a>). For example, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nerve_of_a_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Nerve of a category"">nerve of a category</a> satisfies the condition and thus can be considered as an ∞-category.
"
"initial (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An object <i>A</i> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Initial_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Initial object"">initial</a> if there is exactly one morphism from <i>A</i> to each object; e.g., <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empty_set"" title=""Empty set"">empty set</a> in <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_sets"" title=""Category of sets"">Set</a></b>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An object <i>A</i> in an ∞-category <i>C</i> is initial if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{C}(A,B)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>B</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{C}(A,B)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/88632c60099f646c43f42831070f3468005f9cbd"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.418ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Map} _{C}(A,B)""/></span> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contractible_space"" title=""Contractible space"">contractible</a> for each object <i>B</i> in <i>C</i>.</dd>
"
"injective (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An object <i>A</i> in an abelian category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Injective_object"" title=""Injective object"">injective</a> if the functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (-,A)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>Hom</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (-,A)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/457e7b81821e4854c980b5a6080a4ef066fcdd91"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.236ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} (-,A)""/></span> is exact. It is the dual of a projective object.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The term “injective limit” is another name for a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_limit"" title=""Direct limit"">direct limit</a>.</dd>
"
"internal Hom (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"

"inverse (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A morphism <i>f</i> is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_function"" title=""Inverse function"">inverse</a> to a morphism <i>g</i> if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle g\circ f}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle g\circ f}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/10b5ad4985af48d0fb7efa3c8afa5ad7d42bfc92"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.589ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""g\circ f""/></span> is defined and is equal to the identity morphism on the codomain of <i>g</i>, and <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f\circ g}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f\circ g}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b2f61ca7838709fbae07dce9c0d513770f10cfae"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.589ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f\circ g""/></span> is defined and equal to the identity morphism on the domain of <i>g</i>. The inverse of <i>g</i> is unique and is denoted by <i>g</i><sup>−1</sup>. <i>f</i> is a left inverse to <i>g</i> if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f\circ g}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f\circ g}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b2f61ca7838709fbae07dce9c0d513770f10cfae"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.589ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f\circ g""/></span> is defined and is equal to the identity morphism on the domain of <i>g</i>, and similarly for a right inverse.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_limit"" title=""Inverse limit"">inverse limit</a> is the limit of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_system"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Inverse system"">inverse system</a>.</dd>
"
"isomorphic (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An object is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isomorphic"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Isomorphic"">isomorphic</a> to another object if there is an isomorphism between them.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A category is isomorphic to another category if there is an isomorphism between them.</dd>
"
"isomorphism (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A morphism <i>f</i> is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isomorphism"" title=""Isomorphism"">isomorphism</a> if there exists an <i>inverse</i> of <i>f</i>."
"Kan complex (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kan_complex"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Kan complex"">Kan complex</a> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fibrant_object"" title=""Fibrant object"">fibrant object</a> in the category of simplicial sets.
"

<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The right Kan extension functor is the right adjoint (if it exists) to <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f^{*}}"">

"
"Ken Brown's lemma (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ken_Brown%27s_lemma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Ken Brown&#39;s lemma (page does not exist)"">Ken Brown's lemma</a> is a lemma in the theory of model categories.
"
"Kleisli category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a monad <i>T</i>, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kleisli_category"" title=""Kleisli category"">Kleisli category</a> of <i>T</i> is the full subcategory of the category of <i>T</i>-algebras (called Eilenberg–Moore category) that consists of free <i>T</i>-algebras."
"lax (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The term ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lax_functor"" title=""Lax functor"">lax functor</a>"" is essentially synonymous with ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudo-functor"" title=""Pseudo-functor"">pseudo-functor</a>"".
"
"length (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
An object in an abelian category is said to have <span id=""finite_length""></span>finite length if it has a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Composition_series"" title=""Composition series"">composition series</a>. The maximum number of proper subobjects in any such composition series is called the <b>length</b> of <i>A</i>.<sup id=""cite_ref-8"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-8"">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
"

For another example, take <i>f</i> to be the identity functor on <i>C</i> and suppose <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle L=\varinjlim _{X\in C}f(X)}"">

"monad (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monad_(category_theory)"" title=""Monad (category theory)"">monad</a> in a category <i>X</i> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoid_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monoid object"">monoid object</a> in the monoidal category of endofunctors of <i>X</i> with the monoidal structure given by composition. For example, given a group <i>G</i>, define an endofunctor <i>T</i> on <b>Set</b> by <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle T(X)=G\times X}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>T</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle T(X)=G\times X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/079886d159c04dcacdb8bea94d74f7ceb267a57f"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.171ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle T(X)=G\times X}""/></span>. Then define the multiplication <i>μ</i> on <i>T</i> as the natural transformation <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \mu :T\circ T\to T}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>&#x03BC;<!-- μ --></mi>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>T</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>T</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>T</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \mu :T\circ T\to T}</annotation>
  </semantics>

and also define the identity map <i>η</i> in the analogous fashion. Then (<i>T</i>, <i>μ</i>, <i>η</i>) constitutes a monad in <b>Set</b>. More substantially, an adjunction between functors <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle F:X\rightleftarrows A:G}"">

        <mi>G</mi>
      </mstyle>

    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle F:X\rightleftarrows A:G}</annotation>

"
"monadic (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An adjunction is said to be <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monadic_adjunction"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monadic adjunction"">monadic</a> if it comes from the monad that it determines by means of the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eilenberg%E2%80%93Moore_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Eilenberg–Moore category"">Eilenberg–Moore category</a> (the category of algebras for the monad).</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A functor is said to be <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monadic_functor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monadic functor"">monadic</a> if it is a constituent of a monadic adjunction.</dd>
"
"monoidal category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoidal_category"" title=""Monoidal category"">monoidal category</a>, also called a tensor category, is a category <i>C</i> equipped with (1) a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bifunctor"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Bifunctor"">bifunctor</a> <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \otimes :C\times C\to C}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mo>&#x2297;<!-- ⊗ --></mo>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \otimes :C\times C\to C}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d28e24da78ac0e7abe5ffffa235241c097ab5d2b"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:15.499ex; height:2.343ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle \otimes :C\times C\to C}""/></span>, (2) an identity object and (3) natural isomorphisms that make ⊗ associative and the identity object an identity for ⊗, subject to certain coherence conditions.
"
"monoid object (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoid_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Monoid object"">monoid object</a> in a monoidal category is an object together with the multiplication map and the identity map that satisfy the expected conditions like associativity. For example, a monoid object in <b>Set</b> is a usual monoid (unital semigroup) and a monoid object in <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_modules"" title=""Category of modules""><i>R</i>-mod</a></b> is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Associative_algebra"" title=""Associative algebra"">associative algebra</a> over a commutative ring <i>R</i>.
"
"monomorphism (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A morphism <i>f</i> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monomorphism"" title=""Monomorphism"">monomorphism</a> (also called monic) if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle g=h}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>h</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle g=h}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/50f4fd70b1200ffb96f9b7dccc5b64296e8da9f4"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.553ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""g=h""/></span> whenever <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f\circ g=f\circ h}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>g</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>h</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f\circ g=f\circ h}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aced36b06004c1fe84cee7ee4647d6d0e3e0e442"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.5ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""f\circ g=f\circ h""/></span>; e.g., an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Injective_function"" title=""Injective function"">injection</a> in <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_sets"" title=""Category of sets"">Set</a></b>. In other words, <i>f</i> is the dual of an epimorphism.
"
"multicategory (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multicategory"" title=""Multicategory"">multicategory</a> is a generalization of a category in which a morphism is allowed to have more than one domain. It is the same thing as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colored_operad"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Colored operad"">colored operad</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-9"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-9"">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
"
"<i>n</i>-category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<div class=""quotebox pullquote floatright"" style=""width:33%;&#32;;""><style data-mw-deduplicate=""TemplateStyles:r887775652"">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:""Times New Roman"",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:"" “ "";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:""Times New Roman"",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:"" ” "";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class=""quotebox-quote left-aligned"" style="""">[T]he issue of comparing definitions of weak <i>n</i>-category is a slippery one, as it is hard to say what it even <i>means</i> for two such definitions to be equivalent. [...] It is widely held that the structure formed by weak <i>n</i>-categories and the functors, transformations, ... between them should be a weak (<i>n</i> + 1)-category; and if this is the case then the question is whether your weak (<i>n</i> + 1)-category of weak <i>n-</i>categories is equivalent to mine—but whose definition of weak (<i>n</i> + 1)-category are we using here...&#160;?</div>
<p><cite class=""left-aligned"" style="""">Tom Leinster,&#32;<a rel=""nofollow"" class=""external text"" href=""http://www.tac.mta.ca/tac/volumes/10/1/10-01abs.html"">A survey of definitions of <i>n</i>-category</a></cite>
</p>
</div><dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strict_n-category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Strict n-category"">strict <i>n</i>-category</a> is defined inductively: a strict 0-category is a set and a strict <i>n</i>-category is a category whose Hom sets are strict (<i>n</i>-1)-categories. Precisely, a strict <i>n</i>-category is a category enriched over strict (<i>n</i>-1)-categories. For example, a strict 1-category is an ordinary category.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The notion of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_n-category"" title=""Weak n-category"">weak <i>n</i>-category</a> is obtained from the strict one by weakening the conditions like associativity of composition to hold only up to <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coherent_isomorphism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Coherent isomorphism"">coherent isomorphisms</a> in the weak sense.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">3.&#160;&#160;One can define an ∞-category as a kind of a colim of <i>n</i>-categories. Conversely, if one has the notion of a (weak) ∞-category (say a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasi-category"" title=""Quasi-category"">quasi-category</a>) in the beginning, then a weak <i>n</i>-category can be defined as a type of a truncated ∞-category.</dd>
"
"natural (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A natural transformation is, roughly, a map between functors. Precisely, given a pair of functors <i>F</i>, <i>G</i> from a category <i>C</i> to category <i>D</i>, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_transformation"" title=""Natural transformation"">natural transformation</a> φ from <i>F</i> to <i>G</i> is a set of morphisms in <i>D</i>
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \{\phi _{x}:F(x)\to G(x)\mid x\in \operatorname {Ob} (C)\}}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mo fence=""false"" stretchy=""false"">{</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- ϕ --></mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>x</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>:</mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>&#x2223;<!-- ∣ --></mo>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
        <mi>Ob</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo fence=""false"" stretchy=""false"">}</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \{\phi _{x}:F(x)\to G(x)\mid x\in \operatorname {Ob} (C)\}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da61c25dbb0472cd348dcfd1ee6f80206e551ab5"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:33.063ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle \{\phi _{x}:F(x)\to G(x)\mid x\in \operatorname {Ob} (C)\}}""/></span></dd></dl>
satisfying the condition: for each morphism <i>f</i>: <i>x</i> → <i>y</i> in <i>C</i>, <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \phi _{y}\circ F(f)=G(f)\circ \phi _{x}}"">

    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">

          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>y</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>&#x2218;<!-- ∘ --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>&#x03D5;<!-- ϕ --></mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>x</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \phi _{y}\circ F(f)=G(f)\circ \phi _{x}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/60ec6093d1998a801af4db2ea8a5acec1868608c"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:22.224ex; height:3.009ex;"" alt=""\phi _{y}\circ F(f)=G(f)\circ \phi _{x}""/></span>. For example, writing <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle GL_{n}(R)}"">

Similarly, <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle R\mapsto R^{*}}"">

    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle R\mapsto R^{*}}</annotation>

Then the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Determinant"" title=""Determinant"">determinant</a> det is a natural transformation from <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle GL_{n}}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>G</mi>
        <msub>
          <mi>L</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>n</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle GL_{n}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a41d6b4f9b104c2e8f659319ddbd61792518ace2"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.628ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""GL_{n}""/></span> to -<sup>*</sup>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_isomorphism"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Natural isomorphism"">natural isomorphism</a> is a natural transformation that is an isomorphism (i.e., admits the inverse).</dd>

<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:95px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nerve-2-simplex.png"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d4/Nerve-2-simplex.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""93"" height=""98"" class=""thumbimage"" data-file-width=""93"" data-file-height=""98"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nerve-2-simplex.png"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div>The composition is encoded as a 2-simplex.</div></div></div>"

"
"normal (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A monomorphism is normal if it is the kernel of some morphism, and an epimorphism is conormal if it is the cokernel of some morphism.  A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normal_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Normal category"">normal</a> if every monomorphism is normal."
"object (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An object is part of a data defining a category.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An [adjective] object in a category <i>C</i> is a contravariant functor (or presheaf) from some fixed category corresponding to the ""adjective"" to <i>C</i>. For example, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Simplicial object"">simplicial object</a> in <i>C</i> is a contravariant functor from the simplicial category to <i>C</i> and a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=%CE%93-object&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Γ-object (page does not exist)"">Γ-object</a> is a pointed contravariant functor from <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=%CE%93_(category_theory)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Γ (category theory) (page does not exist)"">Γ</a> (roughly the pointed category of pointed finite sets) to <i>C</i> provided <i>C</i> is pointed.</dd>
"
"op-fibration (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor π:<i>C</i> → <i>D</i> is an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Op-fibration"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Op-fibration"">op-fibration</a> if, for each object <i>x</i> in <i>C</i> and each morphism <i>g</i>&#160;: π(<i>x</i>) → <i>y</i> in <i>D</i>, there is at least one π-coCartesian morphism <i>f</i>: <i>x</i> → <i>y'</i> in <i>C</i> such that π(<i>f</i>) = <i>g</i>. In other words, π is the dual of a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck_fibration"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Grothendieck fibration"">Grothendieck fibration</a>.
"
"opposite (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposite_category"" title=""Opposite category"">opposite category</a> of a category is obtained by reversing the arrows. For example, if a partially ordered set is viewed as a category, taking its opposite amounts to reversing the ordering."
"perfect (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Sometimes synonymous with ""compact"". See <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perfect_complex"" title=""Perfect complex"">perfect complex</a>.
"
"pointed (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category (or ∞-category) is called pointed if it has a zero object.
"
"polynomial (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A functor from the category of finite-dimensional vector spaces to itself is called a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynomial_functor"" title=""Polynomial functor"">polynomial functor</a> if, for each pair of vector spaces <i>V</i>, <i>W</i>, <span class=""nowrap""><i>F</i>: Hom(<i>V</i>, <i>W</i>) → Hom(<i>F</i>(<i>V</i>), <i>F</i>(<i>W</i>))</span> is a polynomial map between the vector spaces. A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schur_functor"" title=""Schur functor"">Schur functor</a> is a basic example.
"
"preadditive (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preadditive_category"" title=""Preadditive category"">preadditive</a> if it is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enriched_category"" title=""Enriched category"">enriched</a> over the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoidal_category"" title=""Monoidal category"">monoidal category</a> of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abelian_group"" title=""Abelian group"">abelian groups</a>. More generally, it is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preadditive_category#R-linear_categories"" title=""Preadditive category""><i>R</i>-linear</a> if it is enriched over the monoidal category of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Module_(mathematics)"" title=""Module (mathematics)""><i>R</i>-modules</a>, for <i>R</i> a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commutative_ring"" title=""Commutative ring"">commutative ring</a>.
"
"presentable (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regular_cardinal"" title=""Regular cardinal"">regular cardinal</a> κ, a category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Presentabl_category&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Presentabl category (page does not exist)"">κ-presentable</a> if it admits all small colimits and is <a href=""#accessible"">κ-accessible</a>. A category is presentable if it is κ-presentable for some regular cardinal κ (hence presentable for any larger cardinal). <b>Note</b>: Some authors call a presentable category a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Locally_presentable_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Locally presentable category"">locally presentable category</a>.
"
"presheaf (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Another term for a contravariant functor: a functor from a category <i>C</i><sup>op</sup> to <b>Set</b> is a presheaf of sets on <i>C</i> and a functor from <i>C</i><sup>op</sup> to <i>s</i><b>Set</b> is a presheaf of simplicial sets or <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_presheaf"" title=""Simplicial presheaf"">simplicial presheaf</a>, etc. A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck_topology"" title=""Grothendieck topology"">topology</a> on <i>C</i>, if any, tells which presheaf is a sheaf (with respect to that topology).
"
"product (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Product_(category_theory)"" title=""Product (category theory)"">product</a> of a family of objects <i>X</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> in a category <i>C</i> indexed by a set <i>I</i> is the projective limit <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \varprojlim }"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-OP"">
          <munder>
            <mi>lim</mi>
            <mo>&#x2190;<!-- ← --></mo>
          </munder>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \varprojlim }</annotation>
  </semantics>

"
"profunctor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given categories <i>C</i> and <i>D</i>, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Profunctor"" title=""Profunctor"">profunctor</a> (or a distributor) from <i>C</i> to <i>D</i> is a functor of the form <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle D^{\text{op}}\times C\to \mathbf {Set} }"">

    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">

          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mtext>op</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
        <mi>C</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">S</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">e</mi>
          <mi mathvariant=""bold"">t</mi>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle D^{\text{op}}\times C\to \mathbf {Set} }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5c5c81ba3986db2d9df90976554191ad32db811"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:15.863ex; height:2.343ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle D^{\text{op}}\times C\to \mathbf {Set} }""/></span>.
"
"projective (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An object <i>A</i> in an abelian category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Projective_object"" title=""Projective object"">projective</a> if the functor <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (A,-)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>Hom</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (A,-)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dcd09b0dd4114a6f799460830a49b59cb7c3d543"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.236ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} (A,-)""/></span> is exact. It is the dual of an injective object.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;The term “projective limit” is another name for an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_limit"" title=""Inverse limit"">inverse limit</a>.</dd>
"
"PROP (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PROP_(category_theory)"" title=""PROP (category theory)"">PROP</a> is a symmetric strict monoidal category whose objects are natural numbers and whose tensor product <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Addition"" title=""Addition"">addition</a> of natural numbers.
"
"pseudoalgebra (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudoalgebra"" title=""Pseudoalgebra"">pseudoalgebra</a> is a 2-category-version of an algebra for a monad (with a monad replaced by a 2-monad)."
"Quillen (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quillen%E2%80%99s_theorem_A"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Quillen’s theorem A"">Quillen’s theorem A</a> provides a criterion for a functor to be a weak equivalence."
"reflect (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A functor is said to reflect identities if it has the property: if <i>F</i>(<i>k</i>) is an identity then <i>k</i> is an identity as well.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A functor is said to reflect isomorphisms if it has the property:  <i>F</i>(<i>k</i>) is an isomorphism then <i>k</i> is an isomorphism as well.</dd>
"
"representable (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"

"retraction (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<div class=""thumb tright""><div class=""thumbinner"" style=""width:152px;""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Section_retract.svg"" class=""image""><img alt="""" src=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Section_retract.svg/150px-Section_retract.svg.png"" decoding=""async"" width=""150"" height=""166"" class=""thumbimage"" srcset=""//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Section_retract.svg/225px-Section_retract.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Section_retract.svg/300px-Section_retract.svg.png 2x"" data-file-width=""113"" data-file-height=""125"" /></a>  <div class=""thumbcaption""><div class=""magnify""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Section_retract.svg"" class=""internal"" title=""Enlarge""></a></div><i>f</i> is a retraction of <i>g</i>. <i>g</i> is a section of <i>f</i>.</div></div></div>A morphism is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Section_(category_theory)"" title=""Section (category theory)"">retraction</a> if it has a right inverse."
"section (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A morphism is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Section_(category_theory)"" title=""Section (category theory)"">section</a> if it has a left inverse. For example, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axiom_of_choice"" title=""Axiom of choice"">axiom of choice</a> says that any surjective function admits a section.
"
"Segal space (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Segal_space"" title=""Segal space"">Segal spaces</a> were certain simplicial spaces, introduced as models for <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/(infinity,1)-category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""(infinity,1)-category"">(∞,&#160;1)-categories</a>.
"
"semisimple (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
An abelian category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semisimple_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Semisimple category"">semisimple</a> if every short exact sequence splits. For example, a ring is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semisimple_ring"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Semisimple ring"">semisimple</a> if and only if the category of modules over it is semisimple.
"
"Serre functor (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a <i>k</i>-linear category <i>C</i> over a field <i>k</i>, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Serre_functor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Serre functor (page does not exist)"">Serre functor</a> <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:C\to C}"">

"simple object (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A simple object in an abelian category is <span id=""simple_object""></span>an object <i>A</i> that is not isomorphic to the zero object and whose every <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subobject"" title=""Subobject"">subobject</a> is isomorphic to zero or to <i>A</i>. For example, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simple_module"" title=""Simple module"">simple module</a> is precisely a simple object in the category of (say left) modules.
"
"simplex category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplex_category"" title=""Simplex category"">simplex category</a> &#916; is the category where an object is a set [<i>n</i>] = { 0, 1, …, <i>n</i> }, n ≥ 0, totally ordered in the standard way and a morphism is an order-preserving function.
"
"simplicial category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category enriched over simplicial sets.
"
"Simplicial localization (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_localization"" title=""Simplicial localization"">Simplicial localization</a> is a method of localizing a category.
"
"simplicial object (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Simplicial object"">simplicial object</a> in a category <i>C</i> is roughly a sequence of objects <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle X_{0},X_{1},X_{2},\dots }"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mn>0</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>X</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mo>&#x2026;<!-- … --></mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle X_{0},X_{1},X_{2},\dots }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e068505f72a88bf2c295490331817273592e0788"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.761ex; height:2.509ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle X_{0},X_{1},X_{2},\dots }""/></span> in <i>C</i> that forms a simplicial set. In other words, it is a covariant or contravariant functor Δ → <i>C</i>. For example, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_presheaf"" title=""Simplicial presheaf"">simplicial presheaf</a> is a simplicial object in the category of presheaves.
"
"simplicial set (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplicial_set"" title=""Simplicial set"">simplicial set</a> is a contravariant functor from &#916; to <b>Set</b>, where &#916; is the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simplex_category"" title=""Simplex category"">simplex category</a>, a category whose objects are the sets [<i>n</i>] = { 0, 1, …, <i>n</i> } and whose morphisms are order-preserving functions. One writes <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle X_{n}=X([n])}"">

            <mi>n</mi>

"
"site (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category equipped with a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grothendieck_topology"" title=""Grothendieck topology"">Grothendieck topology</a>.
"
"skeletal (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skeleton_(category_theory)"" title=""Skeleton (category theory)"">skeletal</a> if isomorphic objects are necessarily identical.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;A (not unique) <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skeleton_(category_theory)"" title=""Skeleton (category theory)"">skeleton</a> of a category is a full subcategory that is skeletal.</dd>
"
"slice (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given a category <i>C</i> and an object <i>A</i> in it, the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slice_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Slice category"">slice category</a> <i>C</i><sub>/<i>A</i></sub> of <i>C</i> over <i>A</i> is the category whose objects are all the morphisms in <i>C</i> with codomain <i>A</i>, whose morphisms are morphisms in <i>C</i> such that if <i>f</i> is a morphism from <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle p_{X}:X\to A}"">

"
"small (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Small category"">small category</a> is a category in which the class of all morphisms is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_(mathematics)"" title=""Set (mathematics)"">set</a> (i.e., not a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proper_class"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Proper class"">proper class</a>); otherwise <b>large</b>. A category is <b>locally small</b> if the morphisms between every pair of objects <i>A</i> and <i>B</i> form a set. Some authors assume a foundation in which the collection of all classes forms a ""conglomerate"", in which case a <b>quasicategory</b> is a category whose objects and morphisms merely form a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conglomerate_(mathematics)"" title=""Conglomerate (mathematics)"">conglomerate</a>.<sup id=""cite_ref-10"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-10"">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> (NB: some authors use the term ""quasicategory"" with a different meaning.<sup id=""cite_ref-11"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-11"">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>)</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An object in a category is said to be <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Small_object&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Small object (page does not exist)"">small</a> if it is κ-compact for some regular cardinal κ. The notion prominently appears in Quiilen's <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Small_object_argument&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Small object argument (page does not exist)"">small object argument</a> (cf. <a rel=""nofollow"" class=""external free"" href=""https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/small+object+argument"">https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/small+object+argument</a>)</dd>
"
"species (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combinatorial_species"" title=""Combinatorial species"">(combinatorial) species</a> is an endofunctor on the groupoid of finite sets with bijections. It is categorically equivalent to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symmetric_sequence"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Symmetric sequence"">symmetric sequence</a>.
"
"stable (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
An ∞-category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stable_%E2%88%9E-category"" title=""Stable ∞-category"">stable</a> if (1) it has a zero object, (2) every morphism in it admits a fiber and a cofiber and (3) a triangle in it is a fiber sequence if and only if it is a cofiber sequence.
"
"strict (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A morphism <i>f</i> in a category admitting finite limits and finite colimits is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Strict_morphism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Strict morphism (page does not exist)"">strict</a> if the natural morphism <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Coim} (f)\to \operatorname {Im} (f)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>Coim</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>Im</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Coim} (f)\to \operatorname {Im} (f)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1bd6f2101c22c928397f5217eacfe4ff85ef46cd"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.989ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Coim} (f)\to \operatorname {Im} (f)""/></span> is an isomorphism.
"
"strict <i>n</i>-category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A strict 0-category is a set and for any integer <i>n</i> &gt; 0, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strict_n-category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Strict n-category"">strict <i>n</i>-category</a> is a category enriched over strict (<i>n</i>-1)-categories. For example, a strict 1-category is an ordinary category. <b>Note</b>: the term ""<i>n</i>-category"" typically refers to ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_n-category"" title=""Weak n-category"">weak <i>n</i>-category</a>""; not strict one.
"
"subcanonical (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A topology on a category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Subcanonical&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Subcanonical (page does not exist)"">subcanonical</a> if every representable contravariant functor on <i>C</i> is a sheaf with respect to that topology.<sup id=""cite_ref-12"" class=""reference""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glossary_of_category_theory#cite_note-12"">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Generally speaking, some <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flat_topology"" title=""Flat topology"">flat topology</a> may fail to be subcanonical; but flat topologies appearing in practice tend to be subcanonical.
"
"subcategory (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category <i>A</i> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subcategory"" title=""Subcategory"">subcategory</a> of a category <i>B</i> if there is an inclusion functor from <i>A</i> to <i>B</i>.
"
"subobject (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Given an object <i>A</i> in a category, a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subobject"" title=""Subobject"">subobject</a> of <i>A</i> is an equivalence class of monomorphisms to <i>A</i>; two monomorphisms <i>f</i>, <i>g</i> are considered equivalent if <i>f</i> factors through <i>g</i> and <i>g</i> factors through <i>f</i>.
"
"subquotient (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subquotient"" title=""Subquotient"">subquotient</a> is a quotient of a subobject.
"
"subterminal object (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subterminal_object"" title=""Subterminal object"">subterminal object</a> is an object <i>X</i> such that every object has at most one morphism into <i>X</i>.
"
"symmetric monoidal category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symmetric_monoidal_category"" title=""Symmetric monoidal category"">symmetric monoidal category</a> is a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoidal_category"" title=""Monoidal category"">monoidal category</a> (i.e., a category with ⊗) that has maximally symmetric braiding.
"
"symmetric sequence (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symmetric_sequence"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Symmetric sequence"">symmetric sequence</a> is a sequence of objects with actions of <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symmetric_group"" title=""Symmetric group"">symmetric groups</a>. It is categorically equivalent to a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combinatorial_species"" title=""Combinatorial species"">(combinatorial) species</a>.
"
"t-structure (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T-structure"" title=""T-structure"">t-structure</a> is an additional structure on a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triangulated_category"" title=""Triangulated category"">triangulated category</a> (more generally <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stable_%E2%88%9E-category"" title=""Stable ∞-category"">stable ∞-category</a>) that axiomatizes the notions of complexes whose cohomology concentrated in non-negative degrees or non-positive degrees.
"
"Tannakian duality (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tannakian_duality"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Tannakian duality"">Tannakian duality</a> states that, in an appropriate setup, to give a morphism <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle f:X\to Y}"">

        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
        <mi>Y</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle f:X\to Y}</annotation>

In other words, the Hom set <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} (X,Y)}"">

"
"tensor category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
Usually synonymous with <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monoidal_category"" title=""Monoidal category"">monoidal category</a> (though some authors distinguish between the two concepts.)
"
"tensor triangulated category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tensor_triangulated_category&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Tensor triangulated category (page does not exist)"">tensor triangulated category</a> is a category that carries the structure of a symmetric monoidal category and that of a triangulated category in a compatible way.
"

"
"terminal (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;An object <i>A</i> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terminal_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Terminal object"">terminal</a> (also called final) if there is exactly one morphism from each object to <i>A</i>; e.g., <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singleton_(mathematics)"" title=""Singleton (mathematics)"">singletons</a>  in <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_sets"" title=""Category of sets"">Set</a></b>. It is the dual of an <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Initial_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Initial object"">initial object</a>.</dd>
<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;An object <i>A</i> in an ∞-category <i>C</i> is terminal if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{C}(B,A)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <msub>
          <mi>Map</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>B</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Map} _{C}(B,A)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8a813c027b796c2ced18c4ce0cad72c92a2016d5"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.418ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Map} _{C}(B,A)""/></span> is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contractible_space"" title=""Contractible space"">contractible</a> for every object <i>B</i> in <i>C</i>.</dd>
"
"thick subcategory (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A full subcategory of an abelian category is <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Thick_subcategory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1"" class=""new"" title=""Thick subcategory (page does not exist)"">thick</a> if it is closed under extensions.
"
"thin (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thin_category"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Thin category"">thin</a> is a category where there is at most one morphism between any pair of objects.
"
"triangulated category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triangulated_category"" title=""Triangulated category"">triangulated category</a> is a category where one can talk about distinguished triangles, generalization of exact sequences. An abelian category is a prototypical example of a triangulated category. A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derived_category"" title=""Derived category"">derived category</a> is a triangulated category that is not necessary an abelian category.
"
"universal (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"

            </mrow>
          </mover>
        </mrow>
        <mi>f</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>c</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(u_{X},c)\to \operatorname {Hom} _{D}(X,f(c)),\,\alpha \mapsto (X\to f(u_{x}){\overset {f(\alpha )}{\to }}f(c))}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4ad2bafe6189aa1f71cf3e118b146e4ff75c6b84"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:58.947ex; height:4.343ex;"" alt=""\operatorname {Hom} _{C}(u_{X},c)\to \operatorname {Hom} _{D}(X,f(c)),\,\alpha \mapsto (X\to f(u_{x}){\overset {f(\alpha )}{\to }}f(c))""/></span></dd></dl>
is bijective. In particular, if <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(u_{X},-)\simeq \operatorname {Hom} _{D}(X,f(-))}"">

"Waldhausen category (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waldhausen_category"" title=""Waldhausen category"">Waldhausen category</a> is, roughly, a category with families of cofibrations and weak equivalences.
"
"wellpowered (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A category is wellpowered if for each object there is only a set of pairwise non-isomorphic <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subobject"" title=""Subobject"">subobjects</a>."
"Yoneda (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
<dd class=""glossary"">1.&#160;&#160;<div class=""quotebox pullquote floatright"" style=""width:33%;&#32;;""><link rel=""mw-deduplicated-inline-style"" href=""mw-data:TemplateStyles:r887775652""/>
<div class=""quotebox-quote left-aligned"" style="""">Yoneda’s Lemma asserts ... in more evocative terms, a mathematical object X is best thought of in the context of a category surrounding it, and is determined by the network of relations it enjoys with all the objects of that category. Moreover, to understand X it might be more germane to deal directly with the functor representing it. This is reminiscent of Wittgenstein’s ’language game’; i.e., that the meaning of a word is—in essence—determined by, in fact is nothing more than, its relations to all the utterances in a language.</div>
<p><cite class=""left-aligned"" style=""""><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barry_Mazur"" title=""Barry Mazur"">Barry Mazur</a>,&#32;<a rel=""nofollow"" class=""external text"" href=""http://www.math.harvard.edu/~mazur/papers/Thinking.about.Grothendieck%285%29.pdf"">Thinking about Grothendieck</a></cite>
</p>
</div>The <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoneda_lemma"" title=""Yoneda lemma"">Yoneda lemma</a> says: for each set-valued contravariant functor <i>F</i> on <i>C</i> and an object <i>X</i> in <i>C</i>, there is a natural bijection
<dl><dd><span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle F(X)\simeq \operatorname {Nat} (\operatorname {Hom} _{C}(-,X),F)}"">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
      <mstyle displaystyle=""true"" scriptlevel=""0"">
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>&#x2243;<!-- ≃ --></mo>
        <mi>Nat</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>Hom</mi>
          <mrow class=""MJX-TeXAtom-ORD"">
            <mi>C</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">(</mo>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>F</mi>
        <mo stretchy=""false"">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding=""application/x-tex"">{\displaystyle F(X)\simeq \operatorname {Nat} (\operatorname {Hom} _{C}(-,X),F)}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ce9a3b115e08bc0877787d2a8b8b068a09be0dd3"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:29.977ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle F(X)\simeq \operatorname {Nat} (\operatorname {Hom} _{C}(-,X),F)}""/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where Nat means the set of natural transformations. In particular, the functor

</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/28abf5bb4c35aee9919dc9f236e691e90671cec8"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:42.711ex; height:2.843ex;"" alt=""{\displaystyle y:C\to \mathbf {Fct} (C^{\text{op}},\mathbf {Set} ),\,X\mapsto \operatorname {Hom} _{C}(-,X)}""/></span></dd></dl>

<dd class=""glossary"">2.&#160;&#160;If <span class=""mwe-math-element""><span class=""mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y"" style=""display: none;""><math xmlns=""http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML""  alttext=""{\displaystyle F:C\to D}"">

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src=""https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d082755579fdc0f7d9daca655472d59e8347242d"" class=""mwe-math-fallback-image-inline"" aria-hidden=""true"" style=""vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:10.983ex; height:2.176ex;"" alt=""F:C\to D""/></span> is a functor and <i>y</i> is the Yoneda embedding of <i>C</i>, then the <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoneda_extension"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Yoneda extension"">Yoneda extension</a> of <i>F</i> is the left Kan extension of <i>F</i> along <i>y</i>.</dd>"
"zero (Wikipedia Glossary of Category Theory)"¬"
A <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero_object"" class=""mw-redirect"" title=""Zero object"">zero object</a> is an object that is both initial and terminal, such as a <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trivial_group"" title=""Trivial group"">trivial group</a> in <b><a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category_of_groups"" title=""Category of groups"">Grp</a></b>.
"
